2/5/25, 8:43â€¯PM - Aadarsh Tiwari: *Nomination Required - For Trident Information System Center of Excellence (Training followed by PPO) - 2026 Batch*

Dear Students,
Greetings From NIET-CMC !!

This is to inform you all that Trident Information Systems is joining hands with NIET for upskilling, training, OJT and PPO (to performing students) on Microsoft ERP technologies.

Students having knowledge or inclination towards DotNet must register for this Center of Excellence

The Process Flow will be as follows:

Registration process and further shortlisting.
8 weeks classroom training. Classroom training will be online and if physical, then training will be at NIET campus
Followed by 8-10 weeks On Job Training (OJT) at company premises.
After OJT the internship will start in 7th Semester. Stipend will be 15K per month.
During OJT assessment will take place and selected students will get PPO at CTC 3.50 to 4.50 LPA

About Company-
Trident Information Systems is one of the leading IT consulting firms and a trusted Microsoft Dynamics Gold Partner, we believe in nurturing talent and empowering the next generation of professionals. In collaboration with NIET, we are proud to offer an exclusive training program designed to equip students with cutting-edge skills in Microsoft Dynamics 365 (D365) and Business Central (BC).

What is Microsoft ERP (Microsoft Dynamics 365)
Microsoft Dynamics 365 ERP is a cloud-based business solution that integrates essential functions like finance, supply chain, sales, and operations. It helps businesses streamline
processes, improve efficiency, and make informed decisions with advanced analytics and automation.
Financial Management Supply Chain Management Manufacturing, Sales and Marketing
Project Management and Accounting Retail and Commerce
Human Resources Management (HRM) Customer Relationship Management (CRM)

Why Choose Trident?
Industry Leadership: 25+ years of experience in ERP implementation and IT consulting.
Global Reach: Presence in 4 countries (India, UAE, USA, Africa) with 250+ successful customer engagements.
Recognition: Microsoft Dynamics Gold Partner, LS Retail Diamond Partner, and IBM Gold Partner.
Expert Resources: 200+ skilled professionals delivering innovative solutions.

Training Curriculum Overview:
Introduction to Microsoft Dynamics 365 & Business Central Functional Modules: Finance, Supply Chain, Sales & Distribution Real-Time Scenarios and Problem Solving
Advanced Reporting and Analytics Certification and Career Guidance
NOTE - Batch of only 30 students will be formed so register ASAP

Interested Students have to apply at the below link latest by 6th Feb. 2025, till 10.00 AM:

Registration Link  - https://forms.gle/F5hdvtUBQfjBGMou9

ChatGPT said:
Software Requirement Specifications (SRS) and Software Quality Assurance (SQA)
Software Requirement Specifications (SRS) is a crucial document in software engineering that defines the functional and non-functional requirements of a system. It serves as a bridge between stakeholders and developers, ensuring that software is developed according to user needs.

Requirement Engineering Process
The Requirement Engineering Process involves a systematic approach to gathering, analyzing, documenting, and managing software requirements. It ensures that the final product meets stakeholder expectations. The key steps involved are:

1. Elicitation
The process of gathering requirements from stakeholders, users, and domain experts.
Techniques used:
Interviews â€“ One-on-one discussions with users and stakeholders.
Surveys and Questionnaires â€“ Collecting information from a large audience.
Workshops â€“ Collaborative sessions to understand requirements.
Prototyping â€“ Developing initial models to refine requirements.
Observation â€“ Studying how users interact with existing systems.
2. Analysis
Evaluating collected requirements for feasibility, consistency, and completeness.
Identifying conflicts between requirements and resolving them.
Prioritizing requirements based on business needs.
3. Documentation
Writing a structured SRS Document that includes:
Functional Requirements (what the system should do).
Non-functional Requirements (performance, security, usability).
Interface Requirements (hardware/software interaction).
4. Review and Management of User Needs
Continuous validation and verification of requirements with stakeholders.
Managing requirement changes through version control and change request processes.
Feasibility Study
A feasibility study determines whether the project is practical and viable. It includes:

Technical Feasibility â€“ Can the system be developed with available technology?
Economic Feasibility â€“ Is the project cost-effective?
Operational Feasibility â€“ Will users accept and use the system?
Legal Feasibility â€“ Does the system comply with regulations?
Schedule Feasibility â€“ Can it be completed on time?
Information Modelling
Information modelling represents the structure and relationships of data. It helps in understanding system architecture and includes:

Entity-Relationship Diagrams (ERD) â€“ Represents entities, attributes, and relationships.
Class Diagrams â€“ Shows object-oriented classes and relationships.
Use Case Diagram
A Use Case Diagram represents the interactions between users (actors) and the system.
Components:
Actors â€“ Users or external systems interacting with software.
Use Cases â€“ Functionalities of the system.
Relationships â€“ Connections between actors and use cases.
Data Flow Diagrams (DFD)
Represents how data flows through a system.
Levels of DFD:
Level 0 (Context Diagram) â€“ Shows system overview.
Level 1 â€“ Expands main processes.
Level 2+ â€“ Provides detailed breakdowns.
Entity Relationship Diagrams (ERD)
Visual representation of data entities, attributes, and relationships in a database.
Components:
Entities (objects like students, courses).
Attributes (name, ID, etc.).
Relationships (one-to-many, many-to-many).
Decision Tables
A structured way to model business rules and conditions for decision-making.
Used in complex decision scenarios.
SRS Document
The Software Requirement Specification (SRS) document, based on IEEE standards, outlines:

Introduction
Purpose
Scope
Definitions
References
Overall Description
Product perspective
Functions
User characteristics
Constraints
Specific Requirements
Functional
Non-functional
Performance
Security
IEEE Standards for SRS
The IEEE 830-1998 standard defines the recommended structure of an SRS document.
Ensures clarity, completeness, and consistency in requirements.
Software Quality Assurance (SQA)
Software Quality Assurance (SQA) is a process to ensure that the developed software meets quality standards.

Quality Concepts
Quality Control (QC) â€“ Detecting and fixing defects.
Quality Assurance (QA) â€“ Preventing defects through processes.
SQA Activities
Process Definition and Implementation
Reviews and Audits
Testing
Defect Management
Standards Compliance
Formal Approaches to SQA
Inspection â€“ Formal code review.
Walkthroughs â€“ Informal peer review.
Formal Verification â€“ Using mathematical proofs.
Statistical Software Quality Assurance
Uses statistical methods like Six Sigma to measure and improve quality.
Metrics include:
Defect density
Mean time to failure (MTTF)
CMM (Capability Maturity Model)
Defines maturity levels for software development:
Level 1 â€“ Initial (Unpredictable, chaotic).
Level 2 â€“ Repeatable (Basic project management).
Level 3 â€“ Defined (Standardized process).
Level 4 â€“ Managed (Measured and controlled).
Level 5 â€“ Optimizing (Continuous improvement).
ISO Standards for SQA
ISO 9001 â€“ Quality management principles.
ISO/IEC 25010 â€“ Software product quality model.
ISO/IEC 12207 â€“ Software lifecycle processes.
Conclusion

Level	Maturity Stage	Description

2 - Repeatable	Basic Project Management	Establishes basic project management techniques. Repeatable success with process discipline.
3 - Defined	Process Standardization	Organization-wide standardized processes are defined. Defined project frameworks are used.
4 - Managed	Quantitative Management	Uses measurable process metrics for improvement. Data-driven decisions.
5 - Optimizing	Continuous Process Improvement	Focus on continuous improvement with innovative techniques and defect prevention.

Key Aspects of SQA:

Process-Oriented Approach â€“ Ensures every development phase follows quality standards.

ChatGPT said:
Software Requirement Specifications (SRS) and Software Quality Assurance (SQA)
Software Requirement Specifications (SRS) is a crucial document in software engineering that defines the functional and non-functional requirements of a system. It serves as a bridge between stakeholders and developers, ensuring that software is developed according to user needs.

Requirement Engineering Process
The Requirement Engineering Process involves a systematic approach to gathering, analyzing, documenting, and managing software requirements. It ensures that the final product meets stakeholder expectations. The key steps involved are:

1. Elicitation
The process of gathering requirements from stakeholders, users, and domain experts.
Techniques used:
Interviews â€“ One-on-one discussions with users and stakeholders.
Surveys and Questionnaires â€“ Collecting information from a large audience.
Workshops â€“ Collaborative sessions to understand requirements.
Prototyping â€“ Developing initial models to refine requirements.
Observation â€“ Studying how users interact with existing systems.
2. Analysis
Evaluating collected requirements for feasibility, consistency, and completeness.
Identifying conflicts between requirements and resolving them.
Prioritizing requirements based on business needs.
3. Documentation
Writing a structured SRS Document that includes:
Functional Requirements (what the system should do).
Non-functional Requirements (performance, security, usability).
Interface Requirements (hardware/software interaction).
4. Review and Management of User Needs
Continuous validation and verification of requirements with stakeholders.
Managing requirement changes through version control and change request processes.
Feasibility Study
A feasibility study determines whether the project is practical and viable. It includes:

Technical Feasibility â€“ Can the system be developed with available technology?
Economic Feasibility â€“ Is the project cost-effective?
Operational Feasibility â€“ Will users accept and use the system?
Legal Feasibility â€“ Does the system comply with regulations?
Schedule Feasibility â€“ Can it be completed on time?
Information Modelling
Information modelling represents the structure and relationships of data. It helps in understanding system architecture and includes:

Entity-Relationship Diagrams (ERD) â€“ Represents entities, attributes, and relationships.
Class Diagrams â€“ Shows object-oriented classes and relationships.
Use Case Diagram
A Use Case Diagram represents the interactions between users (actors) and the system.
Components:
Actors â€“ Users or external systems interacting with software.
Use Cases â€“ Functionalities of the system.
Relationships â€“ Connections between actors and use cases.
Data Flow Diagrams (DFD)
Represents how data flows through a system.
Levels of DFD:
Level 0 (Context Diagram) â€“ Shows system overview.
Level 1 â€“ Expands main processes.
Level 2+ â€“ Provides detailed breakdowns.
Entity Relationship Diagrams (ERD)
Visual representation of data entities, attributes, and relationships in a database.
Components:
Entities (objects like students, courses).
Attributes (name, ID, etc.).
Relationships (one-to-many, many-to-many).
Decision Tables
A structured way to model business rules and conditions for decision-making.
Used in complex decision scenarios.
SRS Document
The Software Requirement Specification (SRS) document, based on IEEE standards, outlines:

Introduction
Purpose
Scope
Definitions
References
Overall Description
Product perspective
Functions
User characteristics
Constraints
Specific Requirements
Functional
Non-functional
Performance
Security
IEEE Standards for SRS
The IEEE 830-1998 standard defines the recommended structure of an SRS document.
Ensures clarity, completeness, and consistency in requirements.
Software Quality Assurance (SQA)
Software Quality Assurance (SQA) is a process to ensure that the developed software meets quality standards.

Quality Concepts
Quality Control (QC) â€“ Detecting and fixing defects.
Quality Assurance (QA) â€“ Preventing defects through processes.
SQA Activities
Process Definition and Implementation
Reviews and Audits
Testing
Defect Management
Standards Compliance
Formal Approaches to SQA
Inspection â€“ Formal code review.
Walkthroughs â€“ Informal peer review.
Formal Verification â€“ Using mathematical proofs.
Statistical Software Quality Assurance
Uses statistical methods like Six Sigma to measure and improve quality.
Metrics include:
Defect density
Mean time to failure (MTTF)
CMM (Capability Maturity Model)
Defines maturity levels for software development:
Level 1 â€“ Initial (Unpredictable, chaotic).
Level 2 â€“ Repeatable (Basic project management).
Level 3 â€“ Defined (Standardized process).
Level 4 â€“ Managed (Measured and controlled).
Level 5 â€“ Optimizing (Continuous improvement).
ISO Standards for SQA
ISO 9001 â€“ Quality management principles.
ISO/IEC 25010 â€“ Software product quality model.
ISO/IEC 12207 â€“ Software lifecycle processes.
Conclusion
SRS and SQA ensure that software development follows a structured process, leading to high-quality software. Requirement engineering defines system needs, while SQA guarantees adherence to quality standards.

How do you select a single column from a DataFrame?
Answer: df['column_name']

Which method is used to remove duplicate rows?
Answer: df.drop_duplicates()

How do you check the first 5 rows of a DataFrame?
Answer: df.head()

How do you rename columns in Pandas?
Answer: df.rename(columns={'old_name': 'new_name'})

Which function is used to drop a column in Pandas?
Answer: df.drop()

How do you check for missing values in a DataFrame?
Answer: df.isnull()

Which function is used to merge two DataFrames?
Answer: df.merge()

Which method provides basic statistical details of a DataFrame?
Answer: df.describe()

Which function is used to save a DataFrame to a CSV file?
Answer: df.to_csv()

Which Pandas method is used to apply a function to a DataFrame?
Answer: df.apply()

Which data structure in Pandas is used for handling tabular data?
Answer: DataFrame

Which method is used to reset the index of a DataFrame?
Answer: df.reset_index()

Which of the following is used to group data in Pandas?
Answer: df.groupby()

What does df.shape return?
Answer: Number of rows and columns

What is Pandas in Python?
Answer: A data manipulation library

Which method is used to fill missing values?
Answer: df.fillna()

Which function is used to convert a DataFrame to a NumPy array?
Answer: df.to_numpy()

Which function is used to read a CSV file in Pandas?
Answer: read_csv()

Which method sorts a DataFrame by values?
Answer: df.sort_values()

What is a major disadvantage of the Hadoop Distributed File System (HDFS)?

C) It has high latency for small files

In Spark, what happens when an RDD is lost due to a node failure?

B) The RDD is recomputed from lineage information

Which of the following Big Data technologies uses Directed Acyclic Graphs (DAG) for execution?

C) Apache Spark

Which NoSQL database uses column-family storage?

B) Cassandra

In Apache Spark, which transformation results in a narrow dependency?

C) Map

Which of the following is NOT a valid data source for Apache Flume?

D) Machine learning models

In Hadoop, what does the Secondary NameNode do?

B) Stores a copy of HDFS metadata snapshots

What is the primary advantage of Apache Parquet over traditional CSV for storing Big Data?

C) It is a columnar storage format, improving query performance

In Kafka, what is the role of a consumer group?

A) Distributes the data processing load among multiple consumers

Which technique is used in Apache Spark to reduce data shuffle between nodes?

A) Broadcast joins

Which component of Hadoop is responsible for tracking resource allocation?

A) YARN ResourceManager

What is the default size of a block in HDFS?

B) 128 MB

In Hadoop, what happens when a DataNode crashes?

B) NameNode replicates the missing data blocks from other DataNodes

Which of the following is a key advantage of using Apache Drill?

B) No need for pre-defined schema, supporting schema-on-read

Which component of Spark is responsible for scheduling and managing cluster resources?

A) Spark Core

Which of the following databases is best suited for handling large-scale graph-based data?

B) Neo4j

What is the primary function of Apache ZooKeeper in a Big Data ecosystem?

B) Manages configuration and synchronization across distributed applications

In Spark, what does RDD stand for?

B) Resilient Distributed Dataset

What is the purpose of a combiner in MapReduce?

A) Acts as a mini-reducer to optimize data shuffling

What is the main difference between Apache Hive and Apache HBase?

A) Hive is a batch-processing engine, while HBase is a NoSQL database

4/4/25, 11:22â€¯AM - Harsh (Biradari Sec-A): #include <iostream>
#include <vector>
using namespace std;

int countWays(int n) {
    if (n == 1) return 1;
    if (n == 2) return 2;

    vector<long long> dp(n + 1);
    dp[1] = 1;
    dp[2] = 2;

    for (int i = 3; i <= n; ++i) {
        dp[i] = dp[i - 1] + dp[i - 2];
    }

    return dp[n];
}

int main() {
    int n;
    cin >> n;

    cout << countWays(n) << endl;

    return 0;
}
4/4/25, 11:22â€¯AM - Harsh (Biradari Sec-A): #include <iostream>
using namespace std;

// Function to calculate GCD of two numbers
int gcdTwo(int a, int b) {
    while (b != 0) {
        int temp = b;
        b = a % b;
        a = temp;
    }
    return a;
}

// Main function to calculate GCD of three numbers
int main() {
    int a, b, c;
    cout << "Enter three numbers: ";
    cin >> a >> b >> c;

    int result = gcdTwo(a, b);   // GCD of first two
    result = gcdTwo(result, c);  // GCD of result and third

    cout << "GCD of " << a << ", " << b << ", and " << c << " is: " << result << endl;

    return 0;
}

4/19/25, 2:00â€¯AM - Deepak (Niet): import java.util.*;
class Node{
    int data;
    Node next;
    Node(int data){
        this.data = data;
        this.next=null;
    }
}
public class Main {
    public static Node read(Scanner sc){
        int n = sc.nextInt();
        if(n == -1){
            return null;
        }
        Node head = new Node(n);
        Node curr = head;
        while (true) {
            n = sc.nextInt();
            if (n == -1) break;
            curr.next = new Node(n);
            curr = curr.next;
        }
        return head;
    }
    public static Node remove(Node head){
        Node dummy = new Node(-1);
        dummy.next = head;
        Node prev = dummy;
        while(head != null){
            if(head.next != null && head.data == head.next.data){
                while(head.next != null && head.data == head.next.data){
                    head = head.next;
                }
                prev.next = head;
                prev = head;
            }
            else{
                prev = head;
            }
            head = head.next;

        }
        return dummy.next;
    }
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);
        Node head = read(sc);
        Node res = remove(head);
        while(res!=null){
            System.out.print(res.data+" ");
            res= res.next;
        }
    }
}

The key elements of a digital strategy include setting clear goals, improving the customer experience, making business processes more efficient, coming up with new ideas for business, and using the right technology to support all of this.

The main pillars of digital transformation are people, process, technology, and data. These are the basic things needed to make digital change successful.

Digital transformation means using digital tools and technologies to make a business work better, faster, and more efficiently.

Absolutely! Here are expanded and simple paragraph-style answers for your questions, aligned with CO4 and appropriate understanding levels:

What are the 4 key challenges of digital transformation?
Digital transformation is not easy, and organizations often face four major challenges. First is resistance to changeâ€”many employees or leaders are used to the old ways and are afraid of new technology. Second is legacy systemsâ€”older software or hardware that cannot easily support modern digital tools. Third, there is often a lack of digital skillsâ€”the workforce may not be trained in using new tools or technologies. Lastly, security and data privacy concerns make it difficult to fully trust digital systems, especially when dealing with customer or sensitive data.

What are the elements of digital strategy?
A good digital strategy has several important parts. It starts with having a clear digital vision or goalâ€”what the business wants to achieve using technology. Then, it focuses on improving customer experience through faster services or personalized communication. It also includes changing internal processes to make work smoother and more efficient. Another element is innovating the business model, which means finding new ways to make money or reach customers using digital tools. Lastly, it involves using the right technology to support all of these goals.

What are the pillars of digital transformation?
Digital transformation stands on four strong pillars. The first is Peopleâ€”employees and leaders who must be ready to accept and drive change. The second is Processâ€”how tasks are done in the organization, which need to become faster and more efficient. The third is Technologyâ€”digital tools, software, and infrastructure that support transformation. The last is Dataâ€”gathering, analyzing, and using data helps in making better decisions and understanding customer behavior.

What is digital transformation in simple words?
Digital transformation simply means using digital technologies like apps, websites, cloud computing, or artificial intelligence to improve how a business works. It helps in making services faster, reducing manual work, and giving better experiences to customers. Itâ€™s about modernizing the way a company operates and delivers value.

What are the barriers that usually block the path to transformation?
Several things can stop or slow down digital transformation. One big barrier is not having a clear vision or planâ€”without knowing where they are going, businesses cannot move forward. Another is lack of leadership supportâ€”if top managers donâ€™t support the change, the team may not take it seriously. Departments working in silos is another issue; if different parts of the company donâ€™t share information, digital tools canâ€™t work effectively. Finally, limited IT infrastructure or outdated systems can also prevent successful transformation.

What is the culture needed for digital transformation?
For digital transformation to succeed, an organization needs a culture that supports change and innovation. People should be open to learning new skills, willing to experiment, and not afraid of making mistakes. Teams should collaborate well, and leaders should encourage new ideas and quick decision-making. A digital culture also means continuously improving and staying updated with the latest technologies.

What is a digital business platform?
A digital business platform is a technology system that helps companies run their operations using digital tools. It brings together different functions like data management, customer service, marketing, and analytics in one place. These platforms allow businesses to integrate systems, automate tasks, and build new services faster. Examples include cloud platforms, customer relationship management (CRM) systems, and e-commerce platforms.

Why would an organization need a digital business platform?
Organizations need a digital business platform to stay competitive and efficient. It helps them deliver services faster, respond to customer needs better, and reduce manual work through automation. Such a platform also allows different departments and systems to work together smoothly. It provides real-time data, supports innovation, and helps the organization grow in a digital world.

What are the most important elements of digital transformation?
The most important elements of digital transformation include leadership commitment, where top management supports and drives change. A strong focus on customer needs is essential to deliver better services. The use of modern technologies like cloud, AI, and data analytics is also critical. Then comes agile processes that allow businesses to quickly adapt to change. Lastly, data-driven decision-making helps organizations to act based on facts, not guesses.

What do you think is a â€œdigital business platformâ€?
A digital business platform is a powerful tool that helps a company manage and run its digital operations. It connects various systems, like finance, marketing, and customer service, into one unified platform. It enables a business to create new digital services, analyze customer data, and automate workflows. In simple terms, it is the backbone that supports all digital activities of a business, helping it to be faster, smarter, and more connected.

Here are the expanded answers in paragraph format for your CO5 Digital Marketing and Transformation questions, written in simple and clear language:

Explain keywords in Digital Marketing. How important is it for SEO?
Keywords are the words or phrases that people type into search engines when they are looking for something. In digital marketing, using the right keywords helps your website show up in search results. For example, if someone searches for â€œbest mobile phone,â€ and your website uses that phrase, it has a better chance of being seen. Keywords are very important for SEO (Search Engine Optimization) because they help search engines understand what your content is about, which can improve your websiteâ€™s ranking and visibility online.

What are the key areas where you can use keywords to optimize your site ranking?
To improve your siteâ€™s ranking, keywords should be used in important places like the title of the page, headings, URL, meta description, and within the content itself. You can also place keywords in image alt text, anchor text, and blog tags. Using keywords correctly in these areas helps search engines understand what your page is about and can increase your chances of appearing in search results.

What are the different types of SEO?
There are mainly three types of SEO.

On-Page SEO focuses on things you can control on your website like content, headings, and keywords.

Off-Page SEO is about actions taken outside your website, like getting backlinks from other websites.

Technical SEO deals with backend improvements such as website speed, mobile-friendliness, and crawlability by search engines. All three types are important to improve your siteâ€™s search performance.

Name some useful Digital Marketing tools.
Some common and helpful digital marketing tools include Google Analytics (for tracking website performance), Google Ads (for paid advertising), SEMrush and Ahrefs (for SEO research), Canva (for creating visuals), Hootsuite (for social media management), and Mailchimp (for email marketing). These tools help marketers plan, execute, and measure their campaigns effectively.

What is meant by digital transformation?
Digital transformation means using modern digital technologies to improve how a business works. It involves changing the way businesses interact with customers, manage operations, and offer services. For example, using online payment systems, automating tasks, or offering customer support through chatbots are all part of digital transformation.

Discuss about Digital Transformation Framework.
A digital transformation framework is a structured plan that helps businesses change using digital technologies. It usually includes important steps like defining a vision, improving customer experience, upgrading technology, changing company culture, and using data for better decisions. This framework acts as a guide to help organizations move smoothly through digital changes and reach their goals.

Discuss the trends in Digital Marketing.
Digital marketing is always changing, and some recent trends include the use of AI and automation, voice search optimization, influencer marketing, video content, and personalized marketing. More companies are using social media platforms and chatbots to connect with customers. Also, mobile-first strategies and data-driven decisions are becoming more popular to improve customer experience and engagement.

Write a note on Digital Revolution.
The digital revolution is the shift from traditional technology to digital technology that began in the late 20th century. It brought huge changes in the way people live, work, and communicate. Examples include the invention of the internet, smartphones, digital media, and cloud computing. It changed industries like education, banking, healthcare, and entertainment by making information and services available anytime and anywhere.

Discuss the barriers that usually block the path to transformation.
Many things can stop or delay digital transformation. These include lack of clear vision, resistance to change, limited digital skills, and old technology systems. Sometimes, departments in a company do not cooperate, which also slows down progress. Another big barrier is concern over data security and privacy, which makes companies afraid to fully go digital.

What is a digital business platform?
A digital business platform is a system that helps businesses connect different digital tools and services. It allows companies to manage their operations online, collect and analyze data, and offer better digital services to customers. For example, platforms like Amazon or Salesforce help businesses run marketing, sales, and customer service all in one place, making work easier and faster.

public class ToggleBits {

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);
        int num = scanner.nextInt();

        if (num < 1 || num > 100) {
            System.out.println("Wrong Input");
        } else {
            int numBits = Integer.toBinaryString(num).length();
            int mask = (1 << numBits) - 1;
            int result = num ^ mask;
            System.out.println(result);
        }
    }
}
6/28/25, 11:33â€¯AM - +91 88811 45073: import java.util.Scanner;

public class RightAlignedNumberPyramid {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);
        System.out.print("Enter a positive integer: ");
        int n = scanner.nextInt();

        for (int i = n; i >= 1; i--) {
            for (int j = 1; j < i; j++) {
                System.out.print(" ");
            }
            for (int j = i; j <= n; j++) {
                System.out.print(j);
            }
            System.out.println();
        }

        scanner.close();
    }
}

7/4/25, 8:19â€¯PM - Rajeev: import java.util.Scanner;

public class MinimumJumps {

    public static int minJumps(int[] arr, int n) {
        if (n <= 1)
            return 0;
        if (arr[0] == 0)
            return -1;

        int maxReach = arr[0];
        int step = arr[0];
        int jump = 1;

        for (int i = 1; i < n; i++) {
            if (i == n - 1)
                return jump;

            maxReach = Math.max(maxReach, i + arr[i]);
            step--;

            if (step == 0) {
                jump++;
                if (i >= maxReach)
                    return -1;
                step = maxReach - i;
            }
        }

        return -1;
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);

        // Read input size
        int n = sc.nextInt();
        int[] arr = new int[n];

        // Read array elements
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            arr[i] = sc.nextInt();
        }

        int result = minJumps(arr, n);
        System.out.println(result);
    }
}
7/4/25, 8:25â€¯PM - Rajeev: import java.util.Scanner;

public class CoinChange {

    // Function to count the number of ways to get the sum
    public static int countWays(int[] coins, int n, int sum) {
        int[] dp = new int[sum + 1];

        // Base case: There is one way to make sum 0 (no coin)
        dp[0] = 1;

        // Iterate over each coin
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            // Update dp[] for all sums from coin[i] to sum
            for (int j = coins[i]; j <= sum; j++) {
                dp[j] += dp[j - coins[i]];
            }
        }

        return dp[sum];
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);

        // Read number of coins
        int n = sc.nextInt();
        int[] coins = new int[n];

        // Read coin denominations
        for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
            coins[i] = sc.nextInt();
        }

        // Read target sum
        int sum = sc.nextInt();

        // Call the function and print result
        System.out.println(countWays(coins, n, sum));
    }
}

7/7/25, 8:14â€¯PM - +91 88811 45073: import java.util.*;

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);
        String s = sc.nextLine();

        List<String> result = new ArrayList<>();
        boolean[] used = new boolean[s.length()];
        char[] chars = s.toCharArray();
        Arrays.sort(chars);

        backtrack(chars, used, new StringBuilder(), result);

        for (String perm : result) {
            System.out.println(perm);
        }
    }

    private static void backtrack(char[] chars, boolean[] used, StringBuilder current, List<String> result) {
        if (current.length() == chars.length) {
            result.add(current.toString());
            return;
        }

        for (int i = 0; i < chars.length; i++) {
            if (used[i]) continue;
            if (i > 0 && chars[i] == chars[i - 1] && !used[i - 1]) continue;

            used[i] = true;
            current.append(chars[i]);
            backtrack(chars, used, current, result);
            current.deleteCharAt(current.length() - 1);
            used[i] = false;
        }
    }
}

            System.out.println("Division by zero is not allowed");

        }
    }
}

public class PhoneNumberValidation {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);
        String phoneNumber = scanner.nextLine();
        scanner.close();

        // Regular expression: starts with 6, 7, 8, or 9 and has exactly 10 digits
        if (phoneNumber.matches("[6789][0-9]{9}")) {
            System.out.println("Valid phone number");
        } else {
            System.out.println("Invalid phone number");
        }
    }
}

public class RomanToInteger {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);
        String s = scanner.nextLine().toUpperCase();
        scanner.close();

        System.out.println(romanToInt(s));
    }

    public static int romanToInt(String s) {
        Map<Character, Integer> romanMap = new HashMap<>();
        romanMap.put('I', 1);
        romanMap.put('V', 5);
        romanMap.put('X', 10);
        romanMap.put('L', 50);
        romanMap.put('C', 100);
        romanMap.put('D', 500);
        romanMap.put('M', 1000);

        int total = 0;
        int prevValue = 0;

        for (int i = s.length() - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
            int currentValue = romanMap.get(s.charAt(i));

            if (currentValue < prevValue) {
                total -= currentValue;
            } else {
                total += currentValue;
            }

            prevValue = currentValue;
        }

        return total;
    }
}

7/19/25, 10:31â€¯PM - Rajeev: from collections import deque

def max_in_subarrays(arr, k):
    n = len(arr)
    q = deque()
    result = []

    for i in range(n):
        # Remove indices out of the current window
        while q and q[0] <= i - k:
            q.popleft()

        # Remove elements smaller than current element
        while q and arr[q[-1]] < arr[i]:
            q.pop()

        q.append(i)

        # Append max of current window to result
        if i >= k - 1:
            result.append(arr[q[0]])

    return result

# -------- USER INPUT --------
n, k = map(int, input("Enter N and K (space separated): ").split())
arr = list(map(int, input(f"Enter {n} elements: ").split()))

# -------- FUNCTION CALL & OUTPUT --------
output = max_in_subarrays(arr, k)
print("Output:", *output)

8/26/25, 6:36â€¯PM - Arpit Jadon: import java.util.*;

public class ChutkiAndBhim {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);
        int t = sc.nextInt();   // number of test cases
        while (t-- > 0) {
            int n = sc.nextInt();
            int evenSum = 0, oddSum = 0;
            for (int i = 0; i < n; i++) {
                int x = sc.nextInt();
                if (x % 2 == 0) evenSum += x;
                else oddSum += x;
            }
            if (evenSum > oddSum) System.out.println("CHUTKI");
            else if (oddSum > evenSum) System.out.println("BHIM");
            else System.out.println("DRAW");
        }
        sc.close();
    }
}
8/26/25, 6:36â€¯PM - Arpit Jadon: 1
8/26/25, 6:36â€¯PM - Arpit Jadon: import java.util.*;

public class ControlPollution {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);
        int N = sc.nextInt();   // number of people
        int X = sc.nextInt();   // smoke per bus
        int Y = sc.nextInt();   // smoke per car
        
        int minSmoke = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
        
        int maxBuses = N / 100;
        for (int buses = 0; buses <= maxBuses; buses++) {
            int remaining = N - buses * 100;
            int cars = (remaining + 3) / 4; // ceil division
            int totalSmoke = buses * X + cars * Y;
            minSmoke = Math.min(minSmoke, totalSmoke);
        }
        
        System.out.println(minSmoke);
        sc.close();
    }
}

1. Problem Statement

Carbon credit markets exist for corporations and industries, but individuals who take sustainable actions (like using EVs, public transport, renewable energy, energy-efficient appliances) get no recognition or financial benefit. This discourages eco-friendly behavior at a personal level.

Thereâ€™s no unified system where an individualâ€™s carbon footprint reduction can be tracked, validated, and monetized.

2. Proposed Solution

Build a MERN + AI/ML app that:

Tracks an individualâ€™s lifestyle footprint (transport, energy, shopping).

Converts their sustainable actions into micro-carbon credits.

Lets users store these credits in a digital wallet.

Enables trading credits for eco-product discounts or converting into green tokens (blockchain-based optional).

3. How It Will Work (Workflow)
Step 1: User Data Collection (Carbon Footprint Sources)

Weâ€™ll get sustainability data via:

EV/Transport Data ğŸš—ğŸš‡

Integration with EV charging stations APIs (e.g., Tata Power EZ Charge, ChargeGrid).

Metro card/Rail card APIs â†’ travel logs = carbon saved vs. personal car.

GPS tracking for ride-sharing/carpooling.

Energy Usage Data âš¡ğŸ 

Link with electricity provider APIs (like Smart Meter dashboards, BSES, Tata Power).

Upload monthly electricity bill PDF â†’ AI parses units consumed.

If usage < average benchmark â†’ credits awarded.

E-commerce & Lifestyle Data ğŸ›’

Partnerships with eco-friendly brands â†’ green product purchases logged.

API integration with payment providers (Razorpay, UPI transaction tagging).

Manual Entry (Fallback) âœï¸

Users can self-log activities (planting trees, recycling, cycling to work).

Verified via photo uploads + geotagging (validated by ML model).

Step 2: Carbon Footprint Calculation (AI/ML Model)

AI model calculates COâ‚‚ saved using baseline data (Government of India emission factors).

Example:

1 km car ride = ~0.120 kg COâ‚‚

1 km metro ride = ~0.035 kg COâ‚‚

Using EV vs. petrol = ~40% lower emissions

Model continuously learns from more data to refine personal carbon profile.

Step 3: Micro-Carbon Credit Allocation

Every kg of COâ‚‚ saved â†’ micro credits.

Example:

Avoid 100 km car ride â†’ save 8.5 kg COâ‚‚ â†’ earn 8.5 credits.

Monthly power bill < average household â†’ bonus credits.

Step 4: Wallet & Marketplace

Users store credits in digital wallet (MongoDB ledger).

Credits can be:

Redeemed for discounts on eco-products (partner brands).

Converted to green tokens on a blockchain marketplace (optional advanced feature).

Donated to NGOs for carbon offset projects (tree plantation, renewable projects).

4. Tech Stack (MERN + AI/ML)

Frontend (React.js) â†’ Carbon Wallet dashboard, eco-savings visualizations, gamified achievements.

Backend (Node.js + Express) â†’ APIs for transaction logging, credit calculation, wallet management.

Database (MongoDB) â†’ Store users, activities, wallet credits.

AI/ML (Python, integrated via Flask/FastAPI microservice):

OCR for electricity bills.

NLP for transaction tagging (â€œEV chargingâ€ vs. â€œPetrol fillingâ€).

Regression model to calculate COâ‚‚ saved.

APIs & Data Sources:

UPI/Payment APIs (Razorpay, Paytm, Google Pay).

EV Charging APIs (Tata Power, Ather Grid, Statiq).

Metro/Transport APIs (DMRC Smart Card, IRCTC future).

Electricity Boards (via bill uploads + OCR parsing).

5. Role-Wise Breakdown

Backend Developer

Build APIs for logging activities, wallet credits, and partner integrations.

Create microservice for AI carbon footprint calculation.

Frontend Developer

Dashboard â†’ daily/weekly/monthly COâ‚‚ saved visualized in charts.

Wallet â†’ gamified view of credits + redeem section.

QA & Testing

Test accuracy of credit calculations.

Simulate fraudulent manual entries (e.g., fake tree photos).

Business Research

Partner with eco-brands (organic stores, EV manufacturers, green startups).

Study carbon credit policies (Indian Govt + UNFCCC).

UI/UX

Gamification â†’ badges like â€œEco Warriorâ€, â€œCarbon Neutral Heroâ€.

Simple and inclusive design for rural & urban users.

6. Expected Impact

Motivates individuals to adopt sustainable lifestyles.

Creates micro-incentives for eco-friendly behavior.

Helps government track citizen-level carbon footprint.

Bridges the gap between corporate carbon credits and individual contributions.

8/30/25, 8:23â€¯PM - Harsh (Biradari Sec-A): Problem Statement

Most individuals struggle to understand where their money goes. Traditional expense tracker apps show basic charts and numbers, but they donâ€™t actively guide users to improve financial habits. There is a lack of personalized, AI-driven financial coaching for individuals in India that can analyze UPI/bank transactions, detect unusual spending patterns, and provide actionable savings advice in real time.
8/30/25, 8:23â€¯PM - Harsh (Biradari Sec-A): Problem Description

In India, UPI and digital banking have become mainstream, generating large volumes of personal transaction data. However:

Users lack financial awareness â†’ They often overspend without realizing it.

Existing apps are passive â†’ They display charts but donâ€™t provide personalized advice.

No peer benchmarking â†’ Users donâ€™t know how their spending compares to others in similar demographics.

No intelligent anomaly detection â†’ Fraudulent or unusual transactions go unnoticed.

This project aims to develop a MERN-based personal finance coach that integrates with UPI/bank APIs, uses AI/ML for expense categorization, and provides a chatbot-like financial coach for personalized tips.

Example:

App detects that the user spent â‚¹5000 on food delivery this month (25% higher than peers).

The AI coach suggests:

â€œYou could save â‚¹1000/month by cooking at home twice a week â€” thatâ€™s â‚¹12,000/year!â€

This bridges the gap between data visualization and financial literacy coaching.
8/30/25, 8:23â€¯PM - Harsh (Biradari Sec-A): Top 3 Skills Our Team Aims to Acquire

AI/ML for Financial Insights

Expense categorization using NLP on transaction text (UPI, SMS, bank statements).

Anomaly detection for unusual spending patterns.

Recommendation models for personalized saving advice.

Full-Stack FinTech Development (MERN + API Integration)

Secure integration with UPI/bank APIs for real-time transaction fetching.

Building a scalable wallet + transaction history dashboard in MERN stack.

Secure handling of user-sensitive data with encryption.

Conversational AI & UX for Finance Coaching

Building a chatbot-like AI finance assistant (similar to ChatGPT but finance-specific).

Designing gamified financial literacy features (badges, savings goals).

Creating a seamless UI/UX that makes financial planning fun and engaging.

1/31/26, 9:08â€¯PM - Harsh (Biradari Sec-A): string solve(const string& input_data) {
    istringstream iss(input_data);

    int N, T;
    iss >> N >> T;

    unordered_map<long long, int> freq;
    long long userId;

    for (int i = 0; i < N; i++) {
        iss >> userId;
        freq[userId]++;
    }

    int count = 0;
    for (auto &p : freq) {
        if (p.second > T) {
            count++;
        }
    }

    return to_string(count);
}
1/31/26, 9:08â€¯PM - Harsh (Biradari Sec-A): string solve(const string& input_data) {
    istringstream iss(input_data);

    int N, K;
    iss >> N >> K;

    vector<long long> arr(N);
    for (int i = 0; i < N; i++) {
        iss >> arr[i];
    }

    unordered_map<long long, int> freq;
    int left = 0, maxLen = 0;

    for (int right = 0; right < N; right++) {
        freq[arr[right]]++;

        while (freq.size() > K) {
            freq[arr[left]]--;
            if (freq[arr[left]] == 0) {
                freq.erase(arr[left]);
            }
            left++;
        }

        maxLen = max(maxLen, right - left + 1);
    }

    return to_string(maxLen);
}
